 Brainstorm a few concrete ideas on how to achieve this task. But only approaches using actions the human can execute! Avoid repeating previously tried approaches.

[trial_imaginator] **Goal:** *Put potato_7 on table_5*  

Below are **alternative ways** the human could reach the same end‑state without re‑using the exact “open → take → move → place” chain you have already tried.  Each plan only uses actions that exist in the domain (move, open, take, place, push/pull, use / break, inspect, etc.) and is described step‑by‑step so you can pick the one that looks most convenient.

---

## Ⅰ  Move the whole chest to the table first  

| Step | Action (human) | Reason / Effect |
|------|----------------|-----------------|
| 1 | `move to (0.0, 0.0)` – stand on the shelf where the chest sits. | Position next to `chest_9`. |
| 2 | `push chest_9 north` (or `pull chest_9 south`) until it rests on `(0.0, 3.0)` – the tile of `table_5`. | The chest is now sitting on the table, so you don’t have to travel to the table later. |
| 3 | `open chest_9` (the chest can be opened wherever it is). | The potato becomes visible. |
| 4 | `take potato_7` (now on the table). | Potato goes into inventory. |
| 5 | `place potato_7 on table_5` (you are already standing on the table tile). | Goal achieved. |
| 6 *(optional)* | `push chest_9 back to its original spot` if you want the room tidy again. | Restores the original layout. |

*Why this is different*: The chest is moved **instead of** the human walking to the table. Only one “move” action (pushing the chest) replaces the series of walking steps.

---

## Ⅱ  Use the key to unlock a locked chest (if you assume the chest has a lock)

| Step | Action | Effect |
|------|--------|--------|
| 1 | `move to (3.0, 1.0)` – go to `key_4`. | Stand on the key. |
| 2 | `take key_4`. | Key in inventory. |
| 3 | `move to (0.0, 0.0)` – back to the chest. | Position at the chest. |
| 4 | `use key_4 on chest_9` (or `unlock chest_9`). | Chest becomes unlocked (if it was locked). |
| 5 | `open chest_9`. | Potato becomes visible. |
| 6 | `take potato_7`. | Potato in inventory. |
| 7 | `move to (0.0, 3.0)` – walk to the table. | Reach the table. |
| 8 | `place potato_7 on table_5`. | Goal achieved. |

*Difference*: We involve a **key‑unlock** step that you have not tried yet; the rest of the flow (open → take → place) stays the same but the unlocking action is new.

---

## Ⅲ  Use the already‑present box as a “transport” device  

| Step | Action | Effect |
|------|--------|--------|
| 1 | `move to (0.0, 2.0)` – stand next to `box_11`. |
| 2 | `open box_11` (the box is open by default, but you can issue the command to be explicit). |
| 3 | `take potato_7` **directly from the chest** (the chest is still at (0.0, 0.0), so you first move there: `move to (0.0, 0.0)`, `open chest_9`, `take potato_7`). |
| 4 | `place potato_7 in box_11`. | Potato now inside the box, which can be moved as a single object. |
| 5 | `move to (0.0, 3.0)` – walk to the table. |
| 6 | `place box_11 on table_5`. | The box sits on the table (still containing the potato). |
| 7 | `open box_11` (if needed) and `take potato_7` from the box. |
| 8 | `place potato_7 on table_5`. | Goal satisfied, and the box remains on the table (optional). |

*Difference*: The potato is **carried inside another container** before reaching the table, avoiding a direct “take → move → place” sequence.

---

## Ⅳ  Break the chest open (if a “break” action exists)

| Step | Action | Effect |
|------|--------|--------|
| 1 | `move to (0.0, 0.0)` – stand by the chest. |
| 2 | `break chest_9` (or `use hammer on chest_9` if a tool is available). | The chest is destroyed, spilling its contents. |
| 3 | `take potato_7` (now lying on the floor). |
| 4 | `move to (0.0, 3.0)` – walk to the table. |
| 5 | `place potato_7 on table_5`. |
| 6 *(optional)* | `remove broken chest pieces` (if the environment lets you clean up). |

*Difference*: No “open” action at all – the chest is **forced open** by breaking it.

---

## Ⅴ  Tele‑hand (if the system supports a “use”‑type remote action)

### How to pick a plan

1. **Check which actions are actually available** in your current simulation (e.g., does `push` work on containers? Is there a `break` command?).

3. **Think about side‑effects** – breaking the chest may leave debris; using the key may be unnecessary if the chest isn’t locked.  
4. **Combine** – you can also mix ideas (e.g., push the chest to the table *and* then break it there).
